## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science – constitutive modeling of thermomechanical behavior
**Analysis**: The variables sigma (stress), epsilon (strain), and T (temperature) describe the mechanical response of a material under deformation at varying temperatures. This is central to solid mechanics, plasticity, and metal forming, where flow stress is modeled as a function of strain hardening and thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Voce saturation: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon) (stress saturates to an upper bound with strain, typical of materials undergoing dynamic recovery)
- Ludwik hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law strain hardening)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 (power-law hardening with pre-strain offset)
- Linear thermal softening of yield: sigma = (c0 - c1 * T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (temperature-dependent yield stress plus hardening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (power-law hardening multiplied by an Arrhenius-like thermal softening factor)
- Temperature-modified modulus: sigma = (c0 - c1 * T) * epsilon (linear thermo-elastic stress, neglecting thermal expansion itself)
- Thermo-plastic additive: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) + c3 * epsilon**c4 (thermal expansion offset combined with nonlinear hardening)
- Johnson–Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * (T - c4)**c5) (multiplicative thermal softening of flow stress, common in impact/temperature models)
- Logarithmic hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * log(c2 + epsilon) + c3 * T (logarithmic strain dependence often seen in large-strain torsion/tension with linear temperature shift)
- Double power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * epsilon**c3 (two-term strain hardening capturing multiple deformation regimes)
- Exponential + power law: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (combined saturating and power-law hardening)
- Arrhenius-coupled power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 / T) (Zener–Hollomon-type temperature dependence, often used in creep and hot working where stress is a function of temperature)
- Inverse temperature softening: sigma = c0 / (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (hyperbolic thermal softening)
- Sigmoidal thermal transition: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 / (1 + exp(c2 * (T - c3))) (abrupt softening across a critical temperature, e.g., phase transformation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening typically follows a power-law with exponent between 0 and 0.5 → epsilon**c with c small positive
- Thermal softening often appears as a multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) that reduces flow stress at higher temperatures
- Saturation of flow stress at large strains is captured by exponential decays: c0 - c1*exp(-c2*epsilon) or hyperbolic forms
- Yield stress common temperature dependence is linear decrease: sigma_y = sigma_y0 - c*(T - T_ref)
- Pre-strain (initial plastic deformation) shifts the effective strain origin: (epsilon0 + epsilon) inside a power law
- Additive decomposition of thermal and mechanical effects: sigma = f(epsilon) + g(T) or sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T)
- Logarithmic strain dependence appears in torsion/tension of ductile metals with large strains: sigma ~ log(epsilon)
- Multiple hardening stages may require sums of power laws or an exponential + power law combination
- Phase transformations can be modeled by a steep sigmoidal factor (e.g., 1/(1+exp(c*(T-crit))) multiplying the flow stress
- When both strain and temperature are present, interactions are often multiplicative, i.e., sigma = h(epsilon) * k(T)
